<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Judicial_appointments">Judicial appointments</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Judicial appointments">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Martin_Van_Buren_judicial_appointments" title="Martin Van Buren judicial appointments" class="mw-redirect">Martin Van Buren judicial appointments</a></div>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Supreme_Court">Supreme Court</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Supreme Court">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Van Buren appointed two Justices to the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_the_United_States" title="Supreme Court of the United States">Supreme Court of the United States</a>:<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/John_McKinley" title="John McKinley">John McKinley</a> – 1838</li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Peter_Vivian_Daniel" title="Peter Vivian Daniel">Peter Vivian Daniel</a> – 1841</li>
</ul>
<p>Van Buren appointed eight other federal judges, all to <a href="/wiki/United_States_district_court" title="United States district court">United States district courts</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Some sources incorrectly state that Van Buren appointed <a href="/wiki/John_Catron" title="John Catron">John Catron</a> to the Supreme Court.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Catron was appointed by Jackson on Jackson's last day in office, and confirmed a few days later, after Van Buren's term had begun.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1840.svg" class="image"><img alt="1840 election returns" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/ElectoralCollege1840.svg/220px-ElectoralCollege1840.svg.png" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/ElectoralCollege1840.svg/330px-ElectoralCollege1840.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c4/ElectoralCollege1840.svg/440px-ElectoralCollege1840.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="612" data-file-height="558" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:ElectoralCollege1840.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Election_of_1840">Election of 1840</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Election of 1840">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Van Buren took the blame for hard times, as Whigs ridiculed him as <i>Martin Van Ruin</i>. Van Buren's rather elegant personal style was also an easy target for Whig attacks, such as the <a href="/wiki/Gold_Spoon_Oration" title="Gold Spoon Oration">Gold Spoon Oration</a>. State elections of 1837 and 1838 were disastrous for the Democrats, and the partial economic recovery in 1838 was offset by a second commercial crisis in that year. Nevertheless, Van Buren controlled his party and was unanimously renominated by the Democrats in 1840. The revolt against Democratic rule led to the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1840" title="United States presidential election, 1840">election</a> of <a href="/wiki/William_Henry_Harrison" title="William Henry Harrison">William Henry Harrison</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_States_Whig_Party" title="United States Whig Party" class="mw-redirect">Whig</a> candidate. Van Buren once mentioned his relief upon leaving office: "As to the presidency, the two happiest days of my life were those of my entrance upon the office and my surrender of it."<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_life">Later life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Later life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mvanburen.jpeg" class="image"><img alt="A three-quarters length painted portrait of a balding man with gray hair, standing with his right hand grasping a bundle of papers lying on a table" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mvanburen.jpeg/220px-Mvanburen.jpeg" width="220" height="294" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mvanburen.jpeg/330px-Mvanburen.jpeg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/af/Mvanburen.jpeg/440px-Mvanburen.jpeg 2x" data-file-width="2242" data-file-height="3000" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mvanburen.jpeg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
1858 portrait by <a href="/wiki/George_Peter_Alexander_Healy" title="George Peter Alexander Healy">GPA Healy</a>, on display at the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>On the expiration of his term, Van Buren returned to his estate, <a href="/wiki/Lindenwald" title="Lindenwald" class="mw-redirect">Lindenwald</a> in Kinderhook, where he planned his return to the White House. He seemed likely to be nominated by the Democrats in 1844, but in April of that year a Van Buren letter to <a href="/wiki/William_H._Hammett" title="William H. Hammett">William H. Hammett</a> was made public.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> In it, Van Buren opposed the immediate annexation of <a href="/wiki/Texas" title="Texas">Texas</a>, but said that he would support annexation once the state of war between Texas and <a href="/wiki/Mexico" title="Mexico">Mexico</a> was resolved.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Van Buren's opposition to immediate annexation cost him the support of pro-slavery Democrats; he began the <a href="/wiki/1844_Democratic_National_Convention" title="1844 Democratic National Convention">Democratic National Convention</a> with a majority of the delegates, but with no southern support he could not reach the two-thirds threshold required for nomination.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> His name was withdrawn after eight ballots, and a <a href="/wiki/Dark_horse" title="Dark horse">dark horse</a>, <a href="/wiki/James_K._Polk" title="James K. Polk">James K. Polk</a>, received the nomination and went on to <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1844" title="United States presidential election, 1844">win the presidency</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg" class="image"><img alt="Half-length photographic portrait of an elderly, balding man dressed in a dark coat, vest and cravat" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg/220px-Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg" width="220" height="267" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/de/Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg/330px-Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/de/Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg 2x" data-file-width="357" data-file-height="434" /></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Martin_Van_Buren_daguerreotype-restored.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Daguerreotype" title="Daguerreotype">Daguerreotype</a> of Martin Van Buren, circa 1855.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Van Buren was increasingly opposed to slavery, and his original attempts to accommodate pro-slavery southerners gave way over time to acceptance of anti-slavery positions including opposing slavery's expansion into newly organized western states.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1848" title="United States presidential election, 1848">In 1848, he was nominated for President</a> by two minor parties, first by the "<a href="/wiki/Barnburner" title="Barnburner" class="mw-redirect">Barnburner</a>" faction of the Democratic Party in New York, then by the <a href="/wiki/Free_Soil_Party" title="Free Soil Party">Free Soil Party</a>, with whom the "Barnburners" coalesced. The Barnburners and Free Soilers opposed Democratic nominee <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Cass" title="Lewis Cass">Lewis Cass</a>, who opposed the <a href="/wiki/Wilmot_Proviso" title="Wilmot Proviso">Wilmot Proviso</a> and was otherwise seen as friendly to slavery.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition, Van Buren, who had been denied the 1844 nomination by Cass supporters despite having begun the convention with a majority of delegates, may have run in order to exact a measure of revenge by denying Cass the presidency.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> Van Buren won no electoral votes, but finished second to <a href="/wiki/Whig_Party_(United_States)" title="Whig Party (United States)">Whig</a> nominee <a href="/wiki/Zachary_Taylor" title="Zachary Taylor">Zachary Taylor</a> in New York, taking enough votes from Cass to give the state—and perhaps the election—to Taylor.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Unlike many anti-slavery Democrats of the 1840s and 1850s, who later joined the <a href="/wiki/Republican_Party_(United_States)" title="Republican Party (United States)">Republican Party</a>, Van Buren and most of his followers remained in the Democratic fold, including his son <a href="/wiki/John_Van_Buren" title="John Van Buren">John Van Buren</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samuel_J._Tilden" title="Samuel J. Tilden">Samuel J. Tilden</a>, who later served as Governor of New York and was the Democratic nominee for <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1876" title="United States presidential election, 1876">President in 1876</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup> Van Buren supported <a href="/wiki/Franklin_Pierce" title="Franklin Pierce">Franklin Pierce</a> for President in 1852, and <a href="/wiki/James_Buchanan" title="James Buchanan">James Buchanan</a> in 1856, though he later opposed the Buchanan administration's efforts to accommodate the southern states when they threatened secession.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1860" title="United States presidential election, 1860">In the election of 1860</a>, he supported <a href="/wiki/Stephen_A._Douglas" title="Stephen A. Douglas">Stephen A. Douglas</a>, the candidate of northern Democrats, and helped create a <a href="/wiki/Electoral_fusion" title="Electoral fusion">fusion ticket</a> in New York of Democratic <a href="/wiki/Electoral_College_(United_States)" title="Electoral College (United States)">electors</a> pledged to both Douglas and <a href="/wiki/John_C._Breckinridge" title="John C. Breckinridge">John C. Breckinridge</a>, but <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a> carried New York and every northern state except <a href="/wiki/New_Jersey" title="New Jersey">New Jersey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> Once the <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">American Civil War</a> began, Van Buren made public his support for the <a href="/wiki/Union_(American_Civil_War)" title="Union (American Civil War)">Union</a>, and supported <a href="/wiki/Abraham_Lincoln" title="Abraham Lincoln">Abraham Lincoln</a>'s efforts to prevent the southern states from seceding.<sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup> In April, 1861 former President Pierce wrote to the other living former Presidents and asked them to consider meeting in order to use their stature and influence to propose a negotiated end to the war. Pierce asked Van Buren to use his role as the senior living ex-President to issue a formal call. Van Buren's reply suggested that Buchanan should be the one to call the meeting, since he was the former President who had served most recently, and nothing more resulted from Pierce's proposal.<sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Van Buren's health began to fail later in 1861, and he was bedridden with pneumonia during the fall and winter of 1861-1862.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> He did not recover, and died of bronchial <a href="/wiki/Asthma" title="Asthma">asthma</a> and <a href="/wiki/Heart_failure" title="Heart failure">heart failure</a> at his Lindenwald estate in Kinderhook at 2:00&#160;a.m. on July 24, 1862 at the age of 79.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> He is buried in the <a href="/wiki/Reformed_Dutch_Church_(Kinderhook,_New_York)" title="Reformed Dutch Church (Kinderhook, New York)">Kinderhook Reformed Dutch Church</a> Cemetery, as are his wife Hannah, his parents, and his son Martin Van Buren, Jr.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Memorials">Memorials</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Memorials">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Counties">Counties</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Counties">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Counties are named for Martin Van Buren in <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_County,_Michigan" title="Van Buren County, Michigan">Michigan</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_County,_Iowa" title="Van Buren County, Iowa">Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_County,_Arkansas" title="Van Buren County, Arkansas">Arkansas</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_County,_Tennessee" title="Van Buren County, Tennessee">Tennessee</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Cass_County,_Missouri" title="Cass County, Missouri">Cass County, Missouri</a> was originally named for Van Buren, and was renamed in 1849 to honor <a href="/wiki/Lewis_Cass" title="Lewis Cass">Lewis Cass</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cities_and_towns">Cities and towns</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Cities and towns">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Cities and towns named for Van Buren include:</p>
<p>Arkansas: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Arkansas" title="Van Buren, Arkansas">Van Buren, Arkansas</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Indiana:<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Indiana" title="Van Buren, Indiana">Van Buren, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Clay_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Clay County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Clay County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Brown_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Brown County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Brown County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Monroe_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Monroe County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Monroe County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Grant_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Grant County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Grant County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Pulaski_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Pulaski County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Pulaski County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Fountain_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Fountain County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Fountain County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_LaGrange_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, LaGrange County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, LaGrange County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Madison_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Madison County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Madison County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Kosciusko_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Kosciusko County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Kosciusko County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Daviess_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Daviess County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Daviess County, Indiana</a><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Shelby_County,_Indiana" title="Van Buren Township, Shelby County, Indiana">Van Buren Township, Shelby County, Indiana</a>.</p>
<p>In addition, Van Buren Township in <a href="/wiki/LaPorte_County,_Indiana" title="LaPorte County, Indiana">LaPorte County, Indiana</a> was later merged with <a href="/wiki/Noble_Township,_LaPorte_County,_Indiana" title="Noble Township, LaPorte County, Indiana">Noble Township</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Iowa: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Jackson_County,_Iowa" title="Van Buren Township, Jackson County, Iowa">Van Buren Township, Jackson County, Iowa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Lee_County,_Iowa" title="Van Buren Township, Lee County, Iowa">Van Buren Township, Lee County, Iowa</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Kentucky: Van Buren, <a href="/wiki/Anderson_County,_Kentucky" title="Anderson County, Kentucky">Anderson County</a>. The small community was abandoned due to the construction and flooding of Taylorsville Lake from 1974 to 1983.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Louisiana: Van Buren, <a href="/wiki/Livingston_Parish,_Louisiana" title="Livingston Parish, Louisiana">Livingston Parish</a>. The original parish seat, it is now abandoned.<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Maine: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Maine" title="Van Buren, Maine">Van Buren, Maine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Michigan: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Charter_Township,_Michigan" title="Van Buren Charter Township, Michigan">Van Buren Charter Township, Michigan</a> and <a href="/wiki/Martin,_Michigan" title="Martin, Michigan">Martin, Michigan</a>. In addition, the now-defunct village of Martinsville in <a href="/wiki/Sumpter_Township,_Michigan" title="Sumpter Township, Michigan">Sumpter Township</a> was named for him.<sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Missouri: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Missouri" title="Van Buren, Missouri">Van Buren, Missouri</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Minnesota: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_St._Louis_County,_Minnesota" title="Van Buren Township, St. Louis County, Minnesota">Van Buren Township, St. Louis County, Minnesota</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Mississippi: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Mississippi" title="Van Buren, Mississippi">Van Buren, Mississippi</a> (defunct).<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>New York: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_New_York" title="Van Buren, New York">Van Buren, New York</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Ohio:<br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Ohio" title="Van Buren, Ohio">Van Buren</a> (a village in <a href="/wiki/Hancock_County,_Ohio" title="Hancock County, Ohio">Hancock County</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Shelby_County,_Ohio" title="Van Buren Township, Shelby County, Ohio">Van Buren Township, Shelby County, Ohio</a>. This township started to be populated by white settlers in the early 1830s. It was incorporated in 1835, and its government organized in 1841.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Putnam_County,_Ohio" title="Van Buren Township, Putnam County, Ohio">Van Buren Township, Putnam County, Ohio</a>. Originally part of <a href="/wiki/Blanchard_Township,_Putnam_County,_Ohio" title="Blanchard Township, Putnam County, Ohio">Blanchard Township</a>, it was surveyed in 1821, became home to its first white settlers in 1835, and was organized in 1843.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Darke_County,_Ohio" title="Van Buren Township, Darke County, Ohio">Van Buren Township, Darke County, Ohio</a><sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup><br />
<a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Township,_Hancock_County,_Ohio" title="Van Buren Township, Hancock County, Ohio">Van Buren Township, Hancock County, Ohio</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Tennessee: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Tennessee" title="Van Buren, Tennessee">Van Buren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Hardeman_County,_Tennessee" title="Hardeman County, Tennessee">Hardeman County</a> (unincorporated). Established in 1831, this unincorporated populated area is located at the intersection of Van Buren and Lake Hardeman Roads, and shares a <a href="/wiki/ZIP_code" title="ZIP code">ZIP code</a> with <a href="/wiki/Hickory_Valley,_Tennessee" title="Hickory Valley, Tennessee">Hickory Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wisconsin: <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren,_Wisconsin" title="Van Buren, Wisconsin">Van Buren</a>, <a href="/wiki/Grant_County,_Wisconsin" title="Grant County, Wisconsin">Grant County</a>. In 1841 this unincorporated area was combined with unincorporated areas named for <a href="/wiki/Gilbert_du_Motier,_Marquis_de_Lafayette" title="Gilbert du Motier, Marquis de Lafayette">Lafayette</a> and <a href="/wiki/Osceola" title="Osceola">Osceola</a> to form the incorporated town of <a href="/wiki/Potosi,_Wisconsin" title="Potosi, Wisconsin">Potosi</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="State_parks">State parks</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: State parks">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_State_Park_(Michigan)" title="Van Buren State Park (Michigan)">Van Buren State Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_Trail_State_Park" title="Van Buren Trail State Park">Van Buren Trail State Park</a><sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup> in Michigan, and Ohio's <a href="/wiki/Van_Buren_State_Park_(Ohio)" title="Van Buren State Park (Ohio)">Van Buren State Park</a> and its Van Buren Lake are named for him.<sup id="cite_ref-167" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mountains">Mountains</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Mountains">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Mount_Van_Buren" title="Mount Van Buren">Mount Van Buren</a> on the <a href="/wiki/Palmer_Land" title="Palmer Land">Palmer Land</a> portion of <a href="/wiki/Antarctica" title="Antarctica">Antarctica</a> was named for Martin Van Buren.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ships">Ships</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Ships">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/USS_Van_Buren_(1839)" title="USS Van Buren (1839)">USS Van Buren</a></i>, a <a href="/wiki/United_States_Navy" title="United States Navy">United States Navy</a> schooner in service from 1839 to 1847 was also named for Martin Van Buren.<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Schools">Schools</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Schools">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Martin_Van_Buren_High_School" title="Martin Van Buren High School">Martin Van Buren High School</a>, <a href="/wiki/Queens_Village" title="Queens Village" class="mw-redirect">Queens Village</a>, NY <sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Martin_Van_Buren&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>During the <a href="/wiki/United_States_presidential_election,_1988" title="United States presidential election, 1988">1988 campaign for President</a>, <a href="/wiki/George_H._W._Bush" title="George H. W. Bush">George H. W. Bush</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Yale_University" title="Yale University">Yale University</a> graduate and member of the <a href="/wiki/Skull_and_Bones" title="Skull and Bones">Skull and Bones</a> secret society, was attempting to become the first sitting Vice President to win election to the Presidency since Van Buren. In the comic strip <i><a href="/wiki/Doonesbury" title="Doonesbury">Doonesbury</a></i> artist <a href="/wiki/Garry_Trudeau" title="Garry Trudeau">Garry Trudeau</a> depicted members of Skull and Bones as attempting to rob Van Buren's grave, apparently intending to use the relics in a ritual that would aid Bush in the election.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>On the television show <i><a href="/wiki/Seinfeld" title="Seinfeld">Seinfeld</a></i>, the episode "<a href="/wiki/The_Van_Buren_Boys" title="The Van Buren Boys">The Van Buren Boys</a>" is about a fictional <a href="/wiki/Street_gang" title="Street gang" class="mw-redirect">street gang</a> that admires Van Buren and bases its rituals and symbols on him, including the hand sign of eight fingers pointing up. Eight fingers signifies Van Buren, the eighth President.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Martin Van Buren was portrayed by <a href="/wiki/Nigel_Hawthorne" title="Nigel Hawthorne">Nigel Hawthorne</a> in the <a href="/wiki/1997_in_film" title="1997 in film">1997</a> <a href="/wiki/List_of_historical_drama_films#Films_set_in_the_18th_and_19th_centuries" title="List of historical drama films" class="mw-redirect">historical drama film</a> <a href="/wiki/Amistad_(film)" title="Amistad (film)"><i>Amistad</i></a>.<sup id="cite_ref-174" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-174"><span>[</span>174<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In an early scene of the film <i><a href="/wiki/Two_Faces_of_January" title="Two Faces of January" class="mw-redirect">Two Faces of January</a></i>, the main characters – American expatriates in <a href="/wiki/Athens" title="Athens">Athens</a> – encounter an American tourist and discover that she is a Van Buren descendant. They then argue over whether Martin Van Buren was the seventh or eighth President.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175"><span>[</span>175<span>]</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-176" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-176"><span>[</span>176<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The <i>USS Van Buren</i> is a fictional Navy aircraft carrier named for President Van Buren which has appeared in the television show <i><a href="/wiki/NCIS:_Los_Angeles" title="NCIS: Los Angeles">NCIS: Los Angeles</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177"><span>[</span>177<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
